<UserId.>111075011801999726475</UserId.>< name>
Lannie Lucier</name>
<Time>1556568758197<//Time>< rating>
4</rating>
< Review>
1. Staff very friendly: Brandee, Erika, Bill, Tim, Danira (new GM) [Front desk]; Maria, Val [housekeeping]; Rigo [maintenance]. (I don't know all the names.)
2. Excellent hot water - for shower, shaving, dishwashing.
3. Traveling w/ dog? Lots of people who travel w/ their pet stay here.
4. In-room AC & heater both work fine & quickly. (It can be quite chilly at night in PS in the wintertime.)
5. Wifi (basic) is fine. I do email, online newspapers frequently on it. YouTube, sports online streaming generally works well.
6. TV: Screen is small, but works well. They have Dish satellite basic pkg. You get, e.g., the 3 local PS traditional broadcast stations; CNN, Fox, several ESPN, etc. About 30 total. That's plenty. Nobody actually needs 200 cable channels!
7. Room has a small, but really quite workable mini-kitchen. Lg fridge w/ freezer. 2 electric "burners." Microwave. Plenty of storage space. As I said above, great hot water. No oven, unfortunately. (Some long-stay guests bring their own counter-top roaster.) No, it's not your kitchen at home, but you can do lots of basic cooking here, plus, of c., it's cheaper than eating out. Front desk has plates, pots, "silver," etc. - kind of mix & match! If you're staying here more than a night or 2, & you like to cook, I'd suggest bringing your own covered 2- or 3-qt pot, plus a deep, covered fry pan, + your must-have basic utensils.
8. Large # of electrical outlets for device-charging.
9. Easily walkable: Rite-Aid pharm. & mini-grocery; Italian deli w/ wonderful bread; 99-Cent Store = (basically) a grocery + dime-store. ¬§ Walkable: Starbucks; Koffi in great PS Mid-Century-style bldg.; Ralph's (lg supermarket); CVS; 2 great bakeries; a # of restaurants.
10. Wonderful views from some of the rooms, + just outside hotel: S. Jacinto Mtns to W & S. Either walk W a bit (to get around Marriott) or 1/2 bl. E (Tahquitz & Sunrise). Great for pics!<//Review>

< Text>
We were there for one night to ride the Tour de Palm Springs so we weren't looking for anything fancy. I loved having the kitchen so I could eat breakfast before attempting to ride the 100 miles that day but other than kitchen the room had nothing but soap. This hotel had to frills at all. The only thing they supplied was toilet paper, hand soap and dish soap. For what we were doing there it wasn't a big deal but if you are staying the weekend make sure to pack the basic stuff the most hotels supply like shampoo and a hair dryer. There was a small stain on my sheet too but it looked like something that the wash machine couldn't get out. YUCK. The people behind the counter were very nice and the grounds seemed pretty clean.</Text>

<Review>Very nice !  First time to a tea spot in San Ramon and found it to be quick & easy. Located very near the bike/walking path - Iron Horse Trail in the shopping center with the Walmart.  Also plenty of parking if you're not walking or biking.
For us, it was the payoff for walking 4K. Smoothie for me, green tea latte for her.
We came back the next day and tried a few snacks - The fried squid, the fried popcorn chicken and the puffs w/red bean.  Everything was tasty. The fried stuff was a bit salty for me. The red bean seemed almost non present except for the color. Of course, this was our first try for snacks in any tea spot and that might be the general standard.
I like this location for its convenience to the path. There is no bike parking in front but there is a few spots at the trail point across - 70 paces approx.  Tthere are a few chairs and 2 small tables in front.
Service was polite, professional and prompt.
I'll visit again when I'm in San Ramon.< /Review><Response>None< /Response></record>

< name>
Paul Cwick (Shveek)</name>
<Date>1570637086948</Date><rate>5< /rate><Review>Best library in the area, in my opinion.  Clean, quiet, well-lighted, well-staffed, spacious, with plenty of computers and plenty of comfortable places to sit (a godsend on hot Summer days, when one needs a quiet place to cool off.)  The small section with tables, where one may eat a lunch, is also nice (I only wish it had more tables, as they fill up quickly.)  The library is also relatively free from unnecessary distractions (such as noisy crazy people), unlike, say, the Sunnyvale Library.  The "Quiet Nook" is another excellent feature of this library, one which I sincerely wish other libraries would adopt:  A nice, quiet, secluded little room by itself with desks equipped with privacy-hutches, and kept mercifully-quiet, for those times when one needs to work free from noise & distractions.  Other useful resources available at this library as well, such as scanners, copiers, etc.  All in all, an excellent library, one which is my first choice for virtually all my library needs.  The only real criticism I can make is the fact that the parking is really not adequate to the needs of the location.  With the numerous special activities going on at either the library, the Swim Center and Central Park, that parking-lot tends to fill up awfully fast and parking soon becomes unavailable (especially when some spaces are blocked-off by Park staff for some bizarre reason.)  There is some underground parking available underneath the library, but it is small & difficult to maneuver in there and also fills up quickly.  What is really needed is a large, multi-level parking-structure for the Library, the Swim Center and Central Park.  I for one would support the construction of such a structure, as I believe it is needed.<//Review>< Pictures>
None</Pictures>
